  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/681059731" />
    <a title="Michael Garrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21787142-michael-garrett"><img alt="Michael Garrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372616209p2/21787142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/681059731?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Garrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Garrett" href="/user/show/21787142-michael-garrett">Michael Garrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer681059731" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16168457721879265764">The story, partly retold from 1956, is set in Berlin from the early 1920s up to and including its occupation by the Allied Forces in May 1945. The overview is from the perspective of two "twin" brothers and their dearest friend, Dagmar. As the story unfolds the reader is drawn into the close and often tense intra-relationship between the three central characters and the inter-relationship of this close group and that of their immediate families, community, city and ultimately the government.<br/>Alth</span>
  <span id="freeText16168457721879265764" style="display:none">The story, partly retold from 1956, is set in Berlin from the early 1920s up to and including its occupation by the Allied Forces in May 1945. The overview is from the perspective of two "twin" brothers and their dearest friend, Dagmar. As the story unfolds the reader is drawn into the close and often tense intra-relationship between the three central characters and the inter-relationship of this close group and that of their immediate families, community, city and ultimately the government.<br />Although, it is fictional, it is based on historical truth as the events of the story such as the Reichstag Fire in 1933 did happen. <br />Since historical fiction is one of my favourite genres, and Ben Elton is a fine writer, I enjoyed the book as he manages to keep the reader absorbed throughout. He also manages to blend humour with sadness in an interesting and thought-provoking way. <br /><br />It is such a shame that many of today's writers and playwrights like Ben Elton, Timothy O'Brien, Bill Bryson are not on the A list of books to be read at GCSE and AS/A levels as surely these writers merit as much attention as those permanently on the list. <br />A young and disaffected teenager from Inner London might find it very difficult to identify with the characters in Jane Austen's novels but can easily identify with the angst of those in Nick Hornby's productions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16168457721879265764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/449061027?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/3444892-shannon">Shannon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449061027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2924674253030810767">Ah, Ben Elton you certainly know how to tug at my heart strings. My fascination with WW2 is so great that of course this is a book I was going to have to read, especially after hearing such great things about it from the publisher's rep.<br/><br/>A Jewish couple have a baby and adopt a German boy who was born on the very same day. Fast forward 15 or so years later when the purge of Jewish blood is being carried out ripping the family and the "twins" apart. Add into this the knowledge we get in the first f</span>
  <span id="freeText2924674253030810767" style="display:none">Ah, Ben Elton you certainly know how to tug at my heart strings. My fascination with WW2 is so great that of course this is a book I was going to have to read, especially after hearing such great things about it from the publisher's rep.<br /><br />A Jewish couple have a baby and adopt a German boy who was born on the very same day. Fast forward 15 or so years later when the purge of Jewish blood is being carried out ripping the family and the "twins" apart. Add into this the knowledge we get in the first few pages in a chapter marked from the year 1956, that one of the brothers didn't survive and you have a story that is guaranteed to have you glued to the page. Which brother? What happens?<br /><br />The ending twists and turns and basically every time I felt like I had finally found my feet again then oops there it all goes again. Initially I found Ben's humorous writing style to be too lighthearted for the dark backdrop that is Germany WW2 era but I certainly came to terms with it and even came to appreciate those moments it brought after being subjected to other more odious scenes.<br /><br />I found this book to be historically fascinating and I even had to hold back tears a few times. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2924674253030810767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Jozef now leads a quiet life as a university professor, but his days of innocence are numbered. With the final tightening of the Nuremberg Race Laws, he loses his job and flees Germany with his younger sister Shoshana. Aided by their Aryan looks and gift for languages, they are recruited into the Jewish resistance to transport orphans across the border into neutral Lithuania. But war soon envelops the continent.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5738.Ben_Elton">About Ben Elton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1637232756152600189">Ben Elton was born on 3 May 1959, in Catford, South London. The youngest of four, he went to Godalming Grammar school, joined amateur dramatic societies and wrote his first play at 15. He wanted to be a stagehand at the local theatre, but instead did A-Level Theatre Studies and studied drama at Manchester University in 1977. <br/><br/>His career as both performer and writer encompasses some of the most memo</span>
  <span id="freeText1637232756152600189" style="display:none">Ben Elton was born on 3 May 1959, in Catford, South London. The youngest of four, he went to Godalming Grammar school, joined amateur dramatic societies and wrote his first play at 15. He wanted to be a stagehand at the local theatre, but instead did A-Level Theatre Studies and studied drama at Manchester University in 1977. <br /><br />His career as both performer and writer encompasses some of the most memorable and incisive comedy of the past twenty years. His ground breaking work as a TV stand-up comedian set the (high) standard of what was to follow. He has received accolades for his hit TV sit-coms, The Young Ones, Blackadder and The Thin Blue Line. <br /><br />More recently he has had successes with three hit West End musicals, including the global phenomenon We Will Rock You. He has written three plays for the London stage, including the multi-award-winning Popcorn. Ben's international bestselling novels include Stark, Inconceivable, Dead Famous and High Society. He won the Crime Writers' Association Gold Dagger Award for the novel Popcorn.<br /><br />Elton lives in Perth with his Aussie wife Sophie and three children.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1637232756152600189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
